</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-below" style="background:#efefef;">
<a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_coloured_voting_box.svg"><img alt="icon" class="noviewer thumbborder" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" decoding="async" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/16px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/24px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/01/A_coloured_voting_box.svg/32px-A_coloured_voting_box.svg.png 2x" width="16"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Politics" title="Portal:Politics">Politics portal</a></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Basic_forms_of_government" title="Template:Basic forms of government"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Basic_forms_of_government" title="Template talk:Basic forms of government"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Basic_forms_of_government&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Anarchism</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Political_philosophy" title="Political philosophy">political philosophy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_movement" title="Political movement">movement</a> that is skeptical of all justifications for <a href="/wiki/Authority" title="Authority">authority</a> and seeks to abolish the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institutions" title="Institutions">institutions</a> they claim maintain unnecessary <a href="/wiki/Coercion" title="Coercion">coercion</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_hierarchy" title="Social hierarchy">hierarchy</a>, typically including, though not necessarily limited to, <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">governments</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">nation states</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESuissa2019b_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESuissa2019b-1">[1]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a>. Anarchism advocates for the replacement of the state with <a href="/wiki/Stateless_society" title="Stateless society">stateless societies</a> or other forms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_association_(communism_and_anarchism)" title="Free association (communism and anarchism)">free associations</a>. As a historically <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left-wing" title="Left-wing">left-wing</a> movement, usually placed on the <a href="/wiki/Far-left_politics" title="Far-left politics">farthest left</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Political_spectrum" title="Political spectrum">political spectrum</a>, it is usually described alongside <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communalism_(Bookchin)" title="Communalism (Bookchin)">communalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Libertarian_Marxism" title="Libertarian Marxism">libertarian Marxism</a> as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libertarian" title="Libertarian">libertarian</a> wing (<a href="/wiki/Libertarian_socialism" title="Libertarian socialism">libertarian socialism</a>) of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist_movement" title="Socialist movement">socialist movement</a>.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humans" title="Humans">Humans</a> lived in <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">societies</a> without formal hierarchies long before the establishment of formal states, <a href="/wiki/Realm" title="Realm">realms</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Empire" title="Empire">empires</a>. With the rise of organised hierarchical bodies, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scepticism" title="Scepticism">scepticism</a> toward authority also rose. Although traces of anarchist thought are found throughout history, modern anarchism emerged from the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a>. During the latter half of the 19th and the first decades of the 20th century, the anarchist movement flourished in most parts of the world and had a significant role in workers' struggles for <a href="/wiki/Emancipation" title="Emancipation">emancipation</a>. Various <a href="/wiki/Anarchist_schools_of_thought" title="Anarchist schools of thought">anarchist schools of thought</a> formed during this period. Anarchists have taken part in several revolutions, most notably in the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Commune" title="Paris Commune">Paris Commune</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, whose end marked the end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_era_of_anarchism" title="Classical era of anarchism">classical era of anarchism</a>. In the last decades of the 20th and into the 21st century, the anarchist movement has been resurgent once more, growing in popularity and influence within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-capitalist" title="Anti-capitalist">anti-capitalist</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-war" title="Anti-war">anti-war</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-globalisation" title="Anti-globalisation">anti-globalisation</a> movements.
</p><p>Anarchism employs a <a href="/wiki/Diversity_of_tactics" title="Diversity of tactics">diversity of tactics</a> in order to meet its ideal ends which can be broadly separated into revolutionary and evolutionary tactics; there is significant overlap between the two, which are merely descriptive. Revolutionary tactics aim to bring down authority and state, having taken a violent turn in the past, while evolutionary tactics aim to prefigure what an anarchist society would be like. Anarchist thought, criticism, and <a href="/wiki/Praxis_(process)" title="Praxis (process)">praxis</a> have played a part in diverse areas of human society.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Etymology,_terminology,_and_definition"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Etymology, terminology, and definition</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>
<ul>

<h2><span id="Etymology.2C_terminology.2C_and_definition"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology,_terminology,_and_definition">Etymology, terminology, and definition</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Definition_of_anarchism_and_libertarianism" title="Definition of anarchism and libertarianism">Definition of anarchism and libertarianism</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_anarchism" title="Glossary of anarchism">Glossary of anarchism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WilhelmWeitling.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2009" data-file-width="1466" decoding="async" height="301" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/WilhelmWeitling.jpg/220px-WilhelmWeitling.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/WilhelmWeitling.jpg/330px-WilhelmWeitling.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/WilhelmWeitling.jpg/440px-WilhelmWeitling.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WilhelmWeitling.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Weitling" title="Wilhelm Weitling">Wilhelm Weitling</a> is an example of a writer who added to anarchist theory without using the exact term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarlson197222–23_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarlson197222–23-2">[2]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The etymological origin of <i>anarchism</i> is from the Ancient Greek <i>anarkhia</i>, meaning "without a ruler", composed of the prefix <i>an-</i> ("without") and the word <i>arkhos</i> ("leader" or "ruler"). The suffix <i><a href="/wiki/-ism" title="-ism">-ism</a></i> denotes the ideological current that favours <a href="/wiki/Anarchy" title="Anarchy">anarchy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates2017128Long2013217_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates2017128Long2013217-3">[3]</a></sup> <i>Anarchism</i> appears in English from 1642 as <i>anarchisme</i> and <i>anarchy</i> from 1539; early English usages emphasised a sense of disorder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMerriam-Webster2019&quot;Anarchism&quot;''Oxford_English_Dictionary''2005&quot;Anarchism&quot;Sylvan2007260_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMerriam-Webster2019&quot;Anarchism&quot;''Oxford_English_Dictionary''2005&quot;Anarchism&quot;Sylvan2007260-4">[4]</a></sup> Various factions within the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> labelled their opponents as <i>anarchists</i>, although few such accused shared many views with later anarchists. Many revolutionaries of the 19th century such as <a href="/wiki/William_Godwin" title="William Godwin">William Godwin</a> (1756–1836) and <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Weitling" title="Wilhelm Weitling">Wilhelm Weitling</a> (1808–1871) would contribute to the anarchist doctrines of the next generation but did not use <i>anarchist</i> or <i>anarchism</i> in describing themselves or their beliefs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoll196427–37_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoll196427–37-5">[5]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first political philosopher to call himself an <i>anarchist</i> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">anarchiste</i>) was <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Joseph_Proudhon" title="Pierre-Joseph Proudhon">Pierre-Joseph Proudhon</a> (1809–1865), marking the formal birth of anarchism in the mid-19th century. Since the 1890s and beginning in France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENettlau1996162_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENettlau1996162-6">[6]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Libertarianism" title="Libertarianism">libertarianism</a></i> has often been used as a synonym for anarchism<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuérin1970"The_Basic_Ideas_of_Anarchism"_7-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuérin1970"The_Basic_Ideas_of_Anarchism"-7'>[7]</a></sup> and its use as a synonym is still common outside the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWard200462Goodway20064Skirda2002183Fernández20099_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWard200462Goodway20064Skirda2002183Fernández20099-8">[8]</a></sup> Some usages of <i>libertarianism</i> refer to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Individualistic" title="Individualistic">individualistic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free-market" title="Free-market">free-market</a> philosophy only, and <a href="/wiki/Free-market_anarchism" title="Free-market anarchism">free-market anarchism</a> in particular is termed <i>libertarian anarchism</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris200261_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris200261-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>While the term <i>libertarian</i> has been largely synonymous with anarchism,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641Cohn20096_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641Cohn20096-10">[10]</a></sup> its meaning has more recently diluted with wider adoption from ideologically disparate groups,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641-11">[11]</a></sup> including both the <a href="/wiki/New_Left" title="New Left">New Left</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libertarian_Marxists" title="Libertarian Marxists">libertarian Marxists</a>, who do not associate themselves with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Authoritarian_socialists" title="Authoritarian socialists">authoritarian socialists</a> or a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vanguard_party" title="Vanguard party">vanguard party</a>, and extreme <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural_liberals" title="Cultural liberals">cultural liberals</a>, who are primarily concerned with <a href="/wiki/Civil_liberties" title="Civil liberties">civil liberties</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641-11">[11]</a></sup> Additionally, some anarchists use <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libertarian_socialist" title="Libertarian socialist">libertarian socialist</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641Chomsky2005123Cohn20096LevyAdams2018104_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641Chomsky2005123Cohn20096LevyAdams2018104-12">[12]</a></sup> to avoid anarchism's negative connotations and emphasise its connections with <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641-11">[11]</a></sup> <i>Anarchism</i> is broadly used to describe the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-authoritarian" title="Anti-authoritarian">anti-authoritarian</a> wing of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist_movement" title="Socialist movement">socialist movement</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevyAdams2018104_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevyAdams2018104-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[nb 1]</a></sup> Anarchism is contrasted to socialist forms which are state-oriented or from above.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOsgood18891_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOsgood18891-19">[18]</a></sup> Scholars of anarchism generally highlight anarchism's socialist credentials<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENewman200515_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENewman200515-20">[19]</a></sup> and criticise attempts at creating dichotomies between the two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris201564_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris201564-21">[20]</a></sup> Some scholars describe anarchism as having many influences from <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberalism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992641-11">[11]</a></sup> and being both liberals and socialists but more so,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalter200244_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalter200244-22">[21]</a></sup> while most scholars reject <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-capitalism" title="Anarcho-capitalism">anarcho-capitalism</a> as a misunderstanding of anarchist principles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992564–565Jennings1993143GayGay199915Morris200813Johnson2008169Franks2013393–394_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992564–565Jennings1993143GayGay199915Morris200813Johnson2008169Franks2013393–394-23">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[nb 2]</a></sup>
</p><p>While <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opposition_to_the_state" title="Opposition to the state">opposition to the state</a> is central to anarchist thought, defining <i>anarchism</i> is not an easy task for scholars, as there is a lot of discussion among scholars and anarchists on the matter, and various currents perceive anarchism slightly differently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELong2013217_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELong2013217-26">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[nb 3]</a></sup> Major definitional elements include the will for a non-coercive society, the rejection of the state apparatus, the belief that human nature allows humans to exist in or progress toward such a non-coercive society, and a suggestion on how to act to pursue the ideal of anarchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLaughlin200725–26_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLaughlin200725–26-30">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_anarchism" title="History of anarchism">History of anarchism</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-modern_era">Pre-modern era</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paolo_Monti_-_Servizio_fotografico_(Napoli,_1969)_-_BEIC_6353768.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="867" decoding="async" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Paolo_Monti_-_Servizio_fotografico_%28Napoli%2C_1969%29_-_BEIC_6353768.jpg/150px-Paolo_Monti_-_Servizio_fotografico_%28Napoli%2C_1969%29_-_BEIC_6353768.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Paolo_Monti_-_Servizio_fotografico_%28Napoli%2C_1969%29_-_BEIC_6353768.jpg/225px-Paolo_Monti_-_Servizio_fotografico_%28Napoli%2C_1969%29_-_BEIC_6353768.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Paolo_Monti_-_Servizio_fotografico_%28Napoli%2C_1969%29_-_BEIC_6353768.jpg/300px-Paolo_Monti_-_Servizio_fotografico_%28Napoli%2C_1969%29_-_BEIC_6353768.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paolo_Monti_-_Servizio_fotografico_(Napoli,_1969)_-_BEIC_6353768.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Zeno_of_Citium" title="Zeno of Citium">Zeno of Citium</a> (c. 334 – c. 262 BC), whose <i><a href="/wiki/Republic_(Zeno)" title="Republic (Zeno)">Republic</a></i> inspired <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kropotkin" title="Peter Kropotkin">Peter Kropotkin</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall199370_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall199370-31">[28]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Before the establishment of towns and cities, an established authority did not exist. It was after the creation of institutions of authority that anarchistic ideas were espoused as a reaction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGraham2005xi–xiv_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGraham2005xi–xiv-32">[29]</a></sup> The most notable precursors to anarchism in the ancient world were in China and Greece. In China, <a href="/wiki/Philosophical_anarchism" title="Philosophical anarchism">philosophical anarchism</a> (the discussion on the legitimacy of the state) was delineated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taoist" title="Taoist">Taoist</a> philosophers <a href="/wiki/Zhuang_Zhou" title="Zhuang Zhou">Zhuang Zhou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laozi" title="Laozi">Laozi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoutinho2016Marshall199354_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoutinho2016Marshall199354-33">[30]</a></sup> Alongside <a href="/wiki/Stoicism" title="Stoicism">Stoicism</a>, Taoism has been said to have had "significant anticipations" of anarchism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESylvan2007257_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESylvan2007257-34">[31]</a></sup>
</p><p>Anarchic attitudes were also articulated by tragedians and philosophers in Greece. <a href="/wiki/Aeschylus" title="Aeschylus">Aeschylus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sophocles" title="Sophocles">Sophocles</a> used the myth of <a href="/wiki/Antigone" title="Antigone">Antigone</a> to illustrate the conflict between rules set by the state and personal <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomy</a>. <a href="/wiki/Socrates" title="Socrates">Socrates</a> questioned Athenian authorities constantly and insisted on the right of individual freedom of conscience. <a href="/wiki/Cynicism_(philosophy)" title="Cynicism (philosophy)">Cynics</a> dismissed human law (<i><a href="/wiki/Nomos_(sociology)" title="Nomos (sociology)">nomos</a></i>) and associated authorities while trying to live according to nature (<i><a href="/wiki/Physis" title="Physis">physis</a></i>). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stoics" title="Stoics">Stoics</a> were supportive of a society based on unofficial and friendly relations among its citizens without the presence of a state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall19934,_66–73_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall19934,_66–73-35">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">medieval Europe</a>, there was no anarchistic activity except some ascetic religious movements. These, and other Muslim movements, later gave birth to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious_anarchism" title="Religious anarchism">religious anarchism</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanian Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazdak" title="Mazdak">Mazdak</a> called for an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egalitarian" title="Egalitarian">egalitarian</a> society and the <a href="/wiki/Abolition_of_monarchy" title="Abolition of monarchy">abolition of monarchy</a>, only to be soon executed by Emperor <a href="/wiki/Kavad_I" title="Kavad I">Kavad I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall199386_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall199386-36">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Basra" title="Basra">Basra</a>, religious sects preached against the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup> In Europe, various sects developed anti-state and libertarian tendencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENettlau19968_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENettlau19968-38">[35]</a></sup> Renewed interest in antiquity during the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> and in private judgment during the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a> restored elements of anti-authoritarian secularism, particularly in France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993108_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993108-39">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> challenges to intellectual authority (secular and religious) and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_revolutions_and_rebellions" title="List of revolutions and rebellions">revolutions of the 1790s and 1848</a> all spurred the ideological development of what became the era of classical anarchism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevyAdams2018307_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevyAdams2018307-40">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span></h3>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, partisan groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Enrag%C3%A9s" title="Enragés">Enragés</a> and the <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr"><a href="/wiki/Sans-culottes" title="Sans-culottes">sans-culottes</a></i></span> saw a turning point in the fermentation of anti-state and federalist sentiments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall19934_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall19934-41">[38]</a></sup> The first anarchist currents developed throughout the 18th century as <a href="/wiki/William_Godwin" title="William Godwin">William Godwin</a> espoused <a href="/wiki/Philosophical_anarchism" title="Philosophical anarchism">philosophical anarchism</a> in England, morally delegitimising the state, <a href="/wiki/Max_Stirner" title="Max Stirner">Max Stirner</a>'s thinking paved the way to <a href="/wiki/Individualist_anarchism" title="Individualist anarchism">individualism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Joseph_Proudhon" title="Pierre-Joseph Proudhon">Pierre-Joseph Proudhon</a>'s theory of <a href="/wiki/Mutualism_(economic_theory)" title="Mutualism (economic theory)">mutualism</a> found fertile soil in France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall19934–5_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall19934–5-42">[39]</a></sup> By the late 1870s, various anarchist schools of thought had become well-defined and a wave of then unprecedented <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Globalisation" title="Globalisation">globalisation</a> occurred from 1880 to 1914.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevy201110–15_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevy201110–15-43">[40]</a></sup> This era of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_anarchism" title="Classical anarchism">classical anarchism</a> lasted until the end of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a> and is considered the golden age of anarchism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall19934–5_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall19934–5-42">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bakunin.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2072" data-file-width="1790" decoding="async" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bakunin.png/170px-Bakunin.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bakunin.png/255px-Bakunin.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Bakunin.png/340px-Bakunin.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bakunin.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mikhail Bakunin opposed the Marxist aim of <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship_of_the_proletariat" title="Dictatorship of the proletariat">dictatorship of the proletariat</a> and allied himself with the federalists in the First International before his expulsion by the Marxists.</div></div></div>
<p>Drawing from mutualism, <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Bakunin" title="Mikhail Bakunin">Mikhail Bakunin</a> founded <a href="/wiki/Collectivist_anarchism" title="Collectivist anarchism">collectivist anarchism</a> and entered the <a href="/wiki/International_Workingmen%27s_Association" title="International Workingmen's Association">International Workingmen's Association</a>, a class worker union later known as the First International that formed in 1864 to unite diverse revolutionary currents. The International became a significant political force, with <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a> being a leading figure and a member of its General Council. Bakunin's faction (the <a href="/wiki/Jura_Federation" title="Jura Federation">Jura Federation</a>) and Proudhon's followers (the mutualists) opposed <a href="/wiki/State_socialism" title="State socialism">state socialism</a>, advocating political <a href="/wiki/Abstentionism" title="Abstentionism">abstentionism</a> and small property holdings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDodson2002312Thomas1985187ChaliandBlin2007116_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDodson2002312Thomas1985187ChaliandBlin2007116-44">[41]</a></sup> After bitter disputes, the Bakuninists were expelled from the International by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxists" title="Marxists">Marxists</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1872_Hague_Congress" title="1872 Hague Congress">1872 Hague Congress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGraham2019334–336Marshall199324_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGraham2019334–336Marshall199324-45">[42]</a></sup> Anarchists were treated similarly in the <a href="/wiki/Second_International" title="Second International">Second International</a>, being ultimately expelled in 1896.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevy201112_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevy201112-46">[43]</a></sup> Bakunin famously predicted that if revolutionaries gained power by Marx's terms, they would end up the new tyrants of workers. In response to their expulsion from the First International, anarchists formed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Imier_International" title="St. Imier International">St. Imier International</a>. Under the influence of <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kropotkin" title="Peter Kropotkin">Peter Kropotkin</a>, a Russian philosopher and scientist, <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-communism" title="Anarcho-communism">anarcho-communism</a> overlapped with collectivism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall19935_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall19935-47">[44]</a></sup> Anarcho-communists, who drew inspiration from the 1871 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Commune" title="Paris Commune">Paris Commune</a>, advocated for free federation and for the distribution of goods according to one's needs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGraham2005xii_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGraham2005xii-48">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>At the turn of the century, anarchism had spread all over the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoya2015327_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoya2015327-49">[46]</a></sup> It was a notable feature of the international syndicalism movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevy201116_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevy201116-50">[47]</a></sup> In China, small groups of students imported the humanistic pro-science version of anarcho-communism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993519–521_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993519–521-51">[48]</a></sup> Tokyo was a hotspot for rebellious youth from countries of the far east, travelling to the Japanese capital to study.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDirlik1991133Ramnath2019681–682_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDirlik1991133Ramnath2019681–682-52">[49]</a></sup> In Latin America, <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_Argentina" title="Anarchism in Argentina">Argentina</a> was a stronghold for <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-syndicalism" title="Anarcho-syndicalism">anarcho-syndicalism</a>, where it became the most prominent left-wing ideology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevy201123Laursen2019157Marshall1993504–508_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevy201123Laursen2019157Marshall1993504–508-53">[50]</a></sup> During this time, a minority of anarchists adopted tactics of revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Political_violence" title="Political violence">political violence</a>. This strategy became known as <a href="/wiki/Propaganda_of_the_deed" title="Propaganda of the deed">propaganda of the deed</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993633–636_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993633–636-54">[51]</a></sup> The dismemberment of the French socialist movement into many groups and the execution and exile of many <a href="/wiki/Communards" title="Communards">Communards</a> to penal colonies following the suppression of the Paris Commune favoured individualist political expression and acts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson2004_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson2004-55">[52]</a></sup> Even though many anarchists distanced themselves from these terrorist acts, infamy came upon the movement and attempts were made to exclude them from American immigration, including the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_Act_of_1903" title="Immigration Act of 1903">Immigration Act of 1903</a>, also called the Anarchist Exclusion Act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993633–636LutzUlmschneider201946_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993633–636LutzUlmschneider201946-56">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Illegalism" title="Illegalism">Illegalism</a> was another strategy which some anarchists adopted during this period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBantman2019374_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBantman2019374-57">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Makhno_group.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="896" data-file-width="1320" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Makhno_group.jpg/220px-Makhno_group.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Makhno_group.jpg/330px-Makhno_group.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Makhno_group.jpg/440px-Makhno_group.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Makhno_group.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nestor Makhno seen with members of the anarchist <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Insurgent_Army_of_Ukraine" title="Revolutionary Insurgent Army of Ukraine">Revolutionary Insurgent Army of Ukraine</a></div></div></div>
<p>Despite concerns, anarchists enthusiastically participated in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> in opposition to the <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">White movement</a>; however, they met harsh suppression after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bolshevik_government" title="Bolshevik government">Bolshevik government</a> was stabilised. Several anarchists from Petrograd and Moscow fled to Ukraine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAvrich2006204_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAvrich2006204-58">[55]</a></sup> notably leading to the <a href="/wiki/Kronstadt_rebellion" title="Kronstadt rebellion">Kronstadt rebellion</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Makhnovshchina" title="Makhnovshchina">Makhnovist movement</a>. With the anarchists being crushed in Russia, two new antithetical currents emerged, namely <a href="/wiki/Platformism" title="Platformism">platformism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Synthesis_anarchism" title="Synthesis anarchism">synthesis anarchism</a>. The former sought to create a coherent group that would push for revolution while the latter were against anything that would resemble a political party. Seeing the victories of the <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolsheviks</a> in the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a> and the resulting <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>, many workers and activists turned to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_parties" title="Communist parties">communist parties</a> which grew at the expense of anarchism and other socialist movements. In France and the United States, members of major syndicalist movements such as the <a href="/wiki/General_Confederation_of_Labour_(France)" title="General Confederation of Labour (France)">General Confederation of Labour</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Workers_of_the_World" title="Industrial Workers of the World">Industrial Workers of the World</a> left their organisations and joined the <a href="/wiki/Communist_International" title="Communist International">Communist International</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENomad196688_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENomad196688-59">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the Spanish Civil War of 1936, anarchists and syndicalists (<a href="/wiki/Confederaci%C3%B3n_Nacional_del_Trabajo" title="Confederación Nacional del Trabajo">CNT</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federaci%C3%B3n_Anarquista_Ib%C3%A9rica" title="Federación Anarquista Ibérica">FAI</a>) once again allied themselves with various currents of leftists. A long tradition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_anarchism" title="Spanish anarchism">Spanish anarchism</a> led to anarchists playing a pivotal role in the war. In response to the army rebellion, an anarchist-inspired movement of peasants and workers, supported by armed militias, took control of Barcelona and of large areas of rural Spain, where they <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collectivised" title="Collectivised">collectivised</a> the land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBolloten19841107_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBolloten19841107-60">[57]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> provided some limited assistance at the beginning of the war, but the result was a bitter fight among communists and anarchists at a series of events named <a href="/wiki/May_Days" title="May Days">May Days</a> as <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> tried to seize control of the <a href="/wiki/Republican_faction_(Spanish_Civil_War)" title="Republican faction (Spanish Civil War)">Republicans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993xi,_466_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993xi,_466-61">[58]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_era">Post-war era</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rojava_Sewing_Cooperative.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2314" data-file-width="3085" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Rojava_Sewing_Cooperative.jpg/220px-Rojava_Sewing_Cooperative.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Rojava_Sewing_Cooperative.jpg/330px-Rojava_Sewing_Cooperative.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Rojava_Sewing_Cooperative.jpg/440px-Rojava_Sewing_Cooperative.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rojava_Sewing_Cooperative.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rojava's support efforts for workers to form cooperatives is exemplified in this sewing cooperative.</div></div></div>
<p>By the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the anarchist movement had been severely weakened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993xi_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993xi-62">[59]</a></sup> The 1960s witnessed a revival of anarchism, likely caused by a perceived failure of <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxism–Leninism</a> and tensions built by the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993539_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993539-63">[60]</a></sup> During this time, anarchism found a presence in other movements critical towards both capitalism and the state such as the <a href="/wiki/Anti-nuclear_movement" title="Anti-nuclear movement">anti-nuclear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_movement" title="Environmental movement">environmental</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peace_movement" title="Peace movement">peace movements</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s" title="Counterculture of the 1960s">counterculture of the 1960s</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/New_Left" title="New Left">New Left</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993xi,_539_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993xi,_539-64">[61]</a></sup> It also saw a transition from its previous revolutionary nature to provocative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-capitalist_reform" title="Anti-capitalist reform">anti-capitalist reformism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevy20115_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevy20115-65">[62]</a></sup> Anarchism became associated with <a href="/wiki/Punk_subculture" title="Punk subculture">punk subculture</a> as exemplified by bands such as <a href="/wiki/Crass" title="Crass">Crass</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sex_Pistols" title="Sex Pistols">Sex Pistols</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993493–494_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993493–494-66">[63]</a></sup> The established <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feminist" title="Feminist">feminist</a> tendencies of <a href="/wiki/Anarcha-feminism" title="Anarcha-feminism">anarcha-feminism</a> returned with vigour during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_wave_of_feminism" title="Second wave of feminism">second wave of feminism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993556–557_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993556–557-67">[64]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Black_anarchism" title="Black anarchism">Black anarchism</a> began to take form at this time and influenced anarchism's move from a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurocentric" title="Eurocentric">Eurocentric</a> demographic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2015680_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2015680-68">[65]</a></sup> This coincided with its failure to gain traction in Northern Europe and its unprecedented height in Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarmon201170_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarmon201170-69">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>Around the turn of the 21st century, anarchism grew in popularity and influence within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-capitalist" title="Anti-capitalist">anti-capitalist</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-war" title="Anti-war">anti-war</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-globalisation" title="Anti-globalisation">anti-globalisation</a> movements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERupert200666_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERupert200666-70">[67]</a></sup> Anarchists became known for their involvement in protests against the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_of_Eight" title="Group of Eight">Group of Eight</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>. During the protests, <i>ad hoc</i> leaderless anonymous cadres known as <a href="/wiki/Black_bloc" title="Black bloc">black blocs</a> engaged in <a href="/wiki/Riot" title="Riot">rioting</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Property_destruction" title="Property destruction">property destruction</a> and violent confrontations with the <a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">police</a>. Other organisational tactics pioneered at this time include <a href="/wiki/Affinity_group" title="Affinity group">affinity groups</a>, <a href="/wiki/Security_culture" title="Security culture">security culture</a> and the use of decentralised technologies such as the Internet. A significant event of this period was the confrontations at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1999_Seattle_WTO_conference" title="1999 Seattle WTO conference">1999 Seattle WTO conference</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERupert200666_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERupert200666-70">[67]</a></sup> Anarchist ideas have been influential in the development of the <a href="/wiki/Zapatista_Army_of_National_Liberation" title="Zapatista Army of National Liberation">Zapatistas</a> in Mexico and the Democratic Federation of Northern Syria, more commonly known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rojava" title="Rojava">Rojava</a>, a <i>de facto</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Permanent_autonomous_zone" title="Permanent autonomous zone">autonomous region</a> in northern Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERamnath2019691_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERamnath2019691-71">[68]</a></sup>
</p><p>While having revolutionary aspirations, many forms of anarchism are not confrontational nowadays. Instead, they are trying to build an alternative way of social organization, based on mutual interdependence and voluntary cooperation. Scholar Carissa Honeywell takes the example of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_not_Bombs" title="Food not Bombs">Food not Bombs</a> group of collectives, to highlight some features of how anarchist groups work: direct action, working together and in solidarity with those left behind. While doing so, they inform about the rising rates of world hunger suggest a policies to tackle hunger, raging from de-funding the arms industry to addressing Monsanto seed-saving policies and patents, helping farmers and commodification of food and housing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoneywell202134–44_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoneywell202134–44-72">[69]</a></sup> Honeywell also emphasizes that contemporary anarchists are interested in the flourishing not only of humans, but non-humans and the environment as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoneywell20211–2_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoneywell20211–2-73">[70]</a></sup> Honeywell argues that escalation of problems such as continuous wars and world poverty show that the current framework not only can not solve those pressing problems for humanity, but are causal factors as well, resulting in the rejection of representative democracy and the state as a whole.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoneywell20211–3_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoneywell20211–3-74">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Thought">Thought</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anarchist_schools_of_thought" title="Anarchist schools of thought">Anarchist schools of thought</a></div>
<p>Anarchist schools of thought have been generally grouped into two main historical traditions, <a href="/wiki/Social_anarchism" title="Social anarchism">social anarchism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Individualist_anarchism" title="Individualist anarchism">individualist anarchism</a>, owing to their different origins, values and evolution.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcLeanMcMillan2003"Anarchism"Ostergaard200314"Anarchism"_75-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcLeanMcMillan2003"Anarchism"Ostergaard200314"Anarchism"-75'>[72]</a></sup> The individualist current emphasises <a href="/wiki/Negative_liberty" title="Negative liberty">negative liberty</a> in opposing restraints upon the free individual, while the social current emphasises <a href="/wiki/Positive_liberty" title="Positive liberty">positive liberty</a> in aiming to achieve the free potential of society through equality and <a href="/wiki/Social_ownership" title="Social ownership">social ownership</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrisonBoyd2003251_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrisonBoyd2003251-76">[73]</a></sup> In a chronological sense, anarchism can be segmented by the classical currents of the late 19th century and the post-classical currents (<a href="/wiki/Anarcha-feminism" title="Anarcha-feminism">anarcha-feminism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_anarchism" title="Green anarchism">green anarchism</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-anarchism" title="Post-anarchism">post-anarchism</a>) developed thereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevyAdams20189_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevyAdams20189-77">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>Beyond the specific factions of anarchist movements which constitute political anarchism lies <a href="/wiki/Philosophical_anarchism" title="Philosophical anarchism">philosophical anarchism</a> which holds that the state lacks moral legitimacy, without necessarily accepting the imperative of revolution to eliminate it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEgoumenides20142_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEgoumenides20142-78">[75]</a></sup> A component especially of individualist anarchism,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOstergaard200312Gabardi1986300–302_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOstergaard200312Gabardi1986300–302-79">[76]</a></sup> philosophical anarchism may tolerate the existence of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minimal_state" title="Minimal state">minimal state</a> but claims that citizens have no <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moral_obligation" title="Moral obligation">moral obligation</a> to obey government when it conflicts with individual autonomy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKlosko20054_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKlosko20054-80">[77]</a></sup> Anarchism pays significant attention to moral arguments since <a href="/wiki/Ethics" title="Ethics">ethics</a> have a central role in anarchist philosophy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFranks2019549_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFranks2019549-81">[78]</a></sup> Anarchism's emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Anti-capitalism" title="Anti-capitalism">anti-capitalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarianism</a>, and for the extension of community and individuality sets it apart from <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-capitalism" title="Anarcho-capitalism">anarcho-capitalism</a> and other types of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economic_libertarian" title="Economic libertarian">economic libertarianism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992564–565Jennings1993143GayGay199915Morris200813Johnson2008169Franks2013393–394_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1992564–565Jennings1993143GayGay199915Morris200813Johnson2008169Franks2013393–394-23">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Anarchism is usually placed on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Far-left" title="Far-left">far-left</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Political_spectrum" title="Political spectrum">political spectrum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrooks1994xiKahn2000Moynihan2007_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrooks1994xiKahn2000Moynihan2007-82">[79]</a></sup> Much of its <a href="/wiki/Anarchist_economics" title="Anarchist economics">economics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anarchist_law" title="Anarchist law">legal philosophy</a> reflect <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-authoritarian" title="Anti-authoritarian">anti-authoritarian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-statist" title="Anti-statist">anti-statist</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libertarian" title="Libertarian">libertarian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Radical_politics" title="Radical politics">radical</a> interpretations of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left-wing" title="Left-wing">left-wing</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socialist" title="Socialist">socialist</a> politics<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuérin197012_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuérin197012-14">[14]</a></sup> such as <a href="/wiki/Collectivist_anarchism" title="Collectivist anarchism">collectivism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-communism" title="Anarcho-communism">communism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Individualist_anarchism" title="Individualist anarchism">individualism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mutualism_(economic_theory)" title="Mutualism (economic theory)">mutualism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-syndicalism" title="Anarcho-syndicalism">syndicalism</a>, among other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Libertarian_socialist" title="Libertarian socialist">libertarian socialist</a> economic theories.<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuérin197035"Critique_of_authoritarian_socialism"_83-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuérin197035"Critique_of_authoritarian_socialism"-83'>[80]</a></sup> As anarchism does not offer a fixed body of doctrine from a single particular worldview,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall199314–17_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall199314–17-84">[81]</a></sup> many anarchist types and traditions exist and varieties of anarchy diverge widely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESylvan2007262_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESylvan2007262-85">[82]</a></sup> One reaction against <a href="/wiki/Sectarianism" title="Sectarianism">sectarianism</a> within the anarchist milieu was <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_without_adjectives" title="Anarchism without adjectives">anarchism without adjectives</a>, a call for toleration and unity among anarchists first adopted by <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Tarrida_del_M%C3%A1rmol" title="Fernando Tarrida del Mármol">Fernando Tarrida del Mármol</a> in 1889 in response to the bitter debates of anarchist theory at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAvrich19966_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAvrich19966-86">[83]</a></sup> Belief in political <a href="/wiki/Nihilism" title="Nihilism">nihilism</a> has been espoused by anarchists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalter200252_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalter200252-87">[84]</a></sup> Despite separation, the various anarchist schools of thought are not seen as distinct entities but rather as tendencies that intermingle and are connected through a set of uniform principles such as individual and local autonomy, mutual aid, network organisation, communal democracy, justified authority and decentralisation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall19931–6AngelbeckGrier2012551_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall19931–6AngelbeckGrier2012551-88">[85]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classical">Classical</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Pierre_Joseph_Proudhon_1865.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1880" data-file-width="1446" decoding="async" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Portrait_of_Pierre_Joseph_Proudhon_1865.jpg/170px-Portrait_of_Pierre_Joseph_Proudhon_1865.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Portrait_of_Pierre_Joseph_Proudhon_1865.jpg/255px-Portrait_of_Pierre_Joseph_Proudhon_1865.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Portrait_of_Pierre_Joseph_Proudhon_1865.jpg/340px-Portrait_of_Pierre_Joseph_Proudhon_1865.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Pierre_Joseph_Proudhon_1865.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pierre-Joseph Proudhon is the primary proponent of mutualism and influenced many future individualist anarchist and social anarchist thinkers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilbur2019216–218_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilbur2019216–218-89">[86]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Inceptive currents among classical anarchist currents were <a href="/wiki/Mutualism_(economic_theory)" title="Mutualism (economic theory)">mutualism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Individualist_anarchism" title="Individualist anarchism">individualism</a>. They were followed by the major currents of <a href="/wiki/Social_anarchism" title="Social anarchism">social anarchism</a> (<a href="/wiki/Collectivist_anarchism" title="Collectivist anarchism">collectivist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-communism" title="Anarcho-communism">communist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-syndicalism" title="Anarcho-syndicalism">syndicalist</a>). They differ on organisational and economic aspects of their ideal society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevyAdams20182_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevyAdams20182-90">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mutualism is an 18th-century economic theory that was developed into anarchist theory by <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Joseph_Proudhon" title="Pierre-Joseph Proudhon">Pierre-Joseph Proudhon</a>. Its aims include <a href="/wiki/Reciprocity_(cultural_anthropology)" title="Reciprocity (cultural anthropology)">reciprocity</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_association_(Marxism_and_anarchism)" title="Free association (Marxism and anarchism)">free association</a>, voluntary <a href="/wiki/Contract" title="Contract">contract</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monetary_reform" title="Monetary reform">monetary reform</a> of both credit and currency that would be regulated by a bank of the people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilbur2019213–218_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilbur2019213–218-91">[88]</a></sup> Mutualism has been retrospectively characterised as ideologically situated between individualist and collectivist forms of anarchism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAvrich19966Miller199111_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAvrich19966Miller199111-92">[89]</a></sup> In <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/What_Is_Property%3F" title="What Is Property?">What Is Property?</a></i> (1840), Proudhon first characterised his goal as a "third form of society, the synthesis of communism and property."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPierson2013187_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPierson2013187-93">[90]</a></sup> Collectivist anarchism is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_socialist" title="Revolutionary socialist">revolutionary socialist</a> form of anarchism<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorris199376_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorris199376-94">[91]</a></sup> commonly associated with <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Bakunin" title="Mikhail Bakunin">Mikhail Bakunin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShannon2019101_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShannon2019101-95">[92]</a></sup> Collectivist anarchists advocate <a href="/wiki/Collective_ownership" title="Collective ownership">collective ownership</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_production" title="Means of production">means of production</a> which is theorised to be achieved through violent revolution<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAvrich19963–4_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAvrich19963–4-96">[93]</a></sup> and that workers be paid according to time worked, rather than goods being distributed according to need as in communism. Collectivist anarchism arose alongside <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a> but rejected the <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship_of_the_proletariat" title="Dictatorship of the proletariat">dictatorship of the proletariat</a> despite the stated Marxist goal of a collectivist <a href="/wiki/Stateless_society" title="Stateless society">stateless society</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeywood2017146–147Bakunin1990_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeywood2017146–147Bakunin1990-97">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Anarcho-communism" title="Anarcho-communism">Anarcho-communism</a> is a theory of anarchism that advocates a <a href="/wiki/Communist_society" title="Communist society">communist society</a> with <a href="/wiki/Common_ownership" title="Common ownership">common ownership</a> of the means of production,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMayne1999131_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMayne1999131-98">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">direct democracy</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Horizontalidad" title="Horizontalidad">horizontal</a> network of <a href="/wiki/Voluntary_association" title="Voluntary association">voluntary associations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_council" title="Workers' council">workers' councils</a> and <a href="/wiki/Worker_cooperative" title="Worker cooperative">worker cooperatives</a>, with production and consumption based on the guiding principle "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/From_each_according_to_his_ability,_to_each_according_to_his_need" title="From each according to his ability, to each according to his need">From each according to his ability, to each according to his need</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993327Turcato2019237–323_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993327Turcato2019237–323-99">[96]</a></sup> Anarcho-communism developed from radical socialist currents after the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGraham2005_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGraham2005-100">[97]</a></sup> but was first formulated as such in the Italian section of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_International" title="First International">First International</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernicone2009111–113_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernicone2009111–113-101">[98]</a></sup> It was later expanded upon in the theoretical work of <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kropotkin" title="Peter Kropotkin">Peter Kropotkin</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETurcato2019239–244_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETurcato2019239–244-102">[99]</a></sup> whose specific style would go onto become the dominating view of anarchists by the late 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevy20116_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevy20116-103">[100]</a></sup> Anarcho-syndicalism is a branch of anarchism that views <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labour_syndicate" title="Labour syndicate">labour syndicates</a> as a potential force for revolutionary social change, replacing capitalism and the state with a new society democratically self-managed by workers. The basic principles of anarcho-syndicalism are <a href="/wiki/Direct_action" title="Direct action">direct action</a>, workers' <a href="/wiki/Solidarity" title="Solidarity">solidarity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_self-management" title="Workers' self-management">workers' self-management</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVan_der_Walt2019249_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVan_der_Walt2019249-104">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p>Individualist anarchism is a set of several traditions of thought within the anarchist movement that emphasise the <a href="/wiki/Individual" title="Individual">individual</a> and their <a href="/wiki/Will_(philosophy)" title="Will (philosophy)">will</a> over any kinds of external determinants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERyley2019225_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyley2019225-105">[102]</a></sup> Early influences on individualist forms of anarchism include <a href="/wiki/William_Godwin" title="William Godwin">William Godwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Max_Stirner" title="Max Stirner">Max Stirner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Henry_David_Thoreau" title="Henry David Thoreau">Henry David Thoreau</a>. Through many countries, individualist anarchism attracted a small yet diverse following of Bohemian artists and intellectuals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993440_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarshall1993440-106">[103]</a></sup> as well as young anarchist outlaws in what became known as <a href="/wiki/Illegalism" title="Illegalism">illegalism</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Individual_reclamation" title="Individual reclamation">individual reclamation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEImrie1994Parry198715_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEImrie1994Parry198715-107">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-classical_and_contemporary">Post-classical and contemporary</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_anarchism" title="Contemporary anarchism">Contemporary anarchism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jarach_and_Zerzan.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Jarach_and_Zerzan.JPG/220px-Jarach_and_Zerzan.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Jarach_and_Zerzan.JPG/330px-Jarach_and_Zerzan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Jarach_and_Zerzan.JPG/440px-Jarach_and_Zerzan.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jarach_and_Zerzan.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lawrence Jarach (left) and <a href="/wiki/John_Zerzan" title="John Zerzan">John Zerzan</a> (right) are two prominent contemporary anarchist authors, with Zerzan being a prominent voice within <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-primitivism" title="Anarcho-primitivism">anarcho-primitivism</a> and Jarach a notable advocate of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Post-left_anarchy" title="Post-left anarchy">post-left anarchy</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Anarchist principles undergird contemporary radical social movements of the left. Interest in the anarchist movement developed alongside momentum in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-globalisation_movement" title="Anti-globalisation movement">anti-globalisation movement</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvren20111_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvren20111-108">[105]</a></sup> whose leading activist networks were anarchist in orientation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvren20112_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvren20112-109">[106]</a></sup> As the movement shaped 21st century radicalism, wider embrace of anarchist principles signaled a revival of interest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvren20112_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvren20112-109">[106]</a></sup> Anarchism has continued to generate many philosophies and movements, at times eclectic, drawing upon various sources and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syncretic" title="Syncretic">combining disparate concepts</a> to create new philosophical approaches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2007303_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2007303-110">[107]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-capitalist" title="Anti-capitalist">anti-capitalist</a> tradition of classical anarchism has remained prominent within contemporary currents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams20184_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams20184-111">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>Contemporary news coverage which emphasizes <a href="/wiki/Black_bloc" title="Black bloc">black bloc</a> demonstrations has reinforced anarchism's historical association with chaos and violence. Its publicity has also led more scholars in fields such as <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropology</a> and <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">history</a> to engage with the anarchist movement, although contemporary anarchism favours actions over academic theory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2010110Evren20111AngelbeckGrier2012549_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2010110Evren20111AngelbeckGrier2012549-112">[109]</a></sup> Various anarchist groups, tendencies, and schools of thought exist today, making it difficult to describe the contemporary anarchist movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFranks2013385–386_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFranks2013385–386-113">[110]</a></sup> While theorists and activists have established "relatively stable constellations of anarchist principles", there is no consensus on which principles are core and commentators describe multiple <i>anarchisms</i>, rather than a singular <i>anarchism</i>, in which common principles are shared between schools of anarchism while each group prioritizes those principles differently. Gender equality can be a common principle, although it ranks as a higher priority to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarcha-feminists" title="Anarcha-feminists">anarcha-feminists</a> than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarcho-communists" title="Anarcho-communists">anarcho-communists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFranks2013386_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFranks2013386-114">[111]</a></sup>
</p><p>Anarchists are generally committed against coercive authority in all forms, namely "all centralized and hierarchical forms of government (e.g., monarchy, representative democracy, state socialism, etc.), economic class systems (e.g., capitalism, Bolshevism, feudalism, slavery, etc.), autocratic religions (e.g., fundamentalist Islam, Roman Catholicism, etc.), patriarchy, heterosexism, white supremacy, and imperialism."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJun2009507–508_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJun2009507–508-115">[112]</a></sup> Anarchist schools disagree on the methods by which these forms should be opposed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJun2009507_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJun2009507-116">[113]</a></sup> The principle of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equal_liberty" title="Equal liberty">equal liberty</a> is closer to anarchist political ethics in that it transcends both the liberal and socialist traditions. This entails that liberty and equality cannot be implemented within the state, resulting in the questioning of all forms of domination and hierarchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEgoumenides201491_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEgoumenides201491-117">[114]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tactics">Tactics</span></h2>
<p>Anarchists' tactics take various forms but in general serve two major goals, namely to first oppose <a href="/wiki/The_Establishment" title="The Establishment">the Establishment</a> and secondly to promote anarchist ethics and reflect an anarchist vision of society, illustrating the unity of means and ends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019107–108_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019107–108-118">[115]</a></sup> A broad categorisation can be made between aims to destroy oppressive states and institutions by revolutionary means on one hand and aims to change society through evolutionary means on the other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams20184–5_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams20184–5-119">[116]</a></sup> Evolutionary tactics embrace <a href="/wiki/Nonviolence" title="Nonviolence">nonviolence</a>, reject violence and take a gradual approach to anarchist aims, although there is significant overlap between the two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinna2019125_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinna2019125-120">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p>Anarchist tactics have shifted during the course of the last century. Anarchists during the early 20th century focused more on strikes and militancy while contemporary anarchists use a broader array of approaches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019112_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019112-121">[118]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_era">Classical era</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:McKinleyAssassination.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="639" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/McKinleyAssassination.jpg/220px-McKinleyAssassination.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/McKinleyAssassination.jpg/330px-McKinleyAssassination.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/McKinleyAssassination.jpg/440px-McKinleyAssassination.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:McKinleyAssassination.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The relationship between <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_and_violence" title="Anarchism and violence">anarchism and violence</a> is a controversial subject among anarchists as shown by anarchist <a href="/wiki/Leon_Czolgosz" title="Leon Czolgosz">Leon Czolgosz</a> <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_William_McKinley" title="Assassination of William McKinley">assassinating</a> <a href="/wiki/William_McKinley" title="William McKinley">William McKinley</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>During the classical era, anarchists had a militant tendency. Not only did they confront state armed forces, as in Spain and Ukraine, but some of them also employed <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a> as <a href="/wiki/Propaganda_of_the_deed" title="Propaganda of the deed">propaganda of the deed</a>. Assassination attempts were carried out against heads of state, some of which were successful. Anarchists also took part in <a href="/wiki/Revolution" title="Revolution">revolutions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019112–113_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019112–113-122">[119]</a></sup> Many anarchists, especially the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galleanists" title="Galleanists">Galleanists</a>, believed that these attempts would be the impetus for a revolution against capitalism and the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorris20207–8_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorris20207–8-123">[120]</a></sup> Many of these attacks were done by individual assailants and the majority took place in the late 1870s, the early 1880s and the 1890s, with some still occurring in the early 1900s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevy201113Nesser201262_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevy201113Nesser201262-124">[121]</a></sup> Their decrease in prevalence was the result of further <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judicial" title="Judicial">judicial</a> power and targeting and cataloging by state institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarmon201155_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarmon201155-125">[122]</a></sup>
</p><p>Anarchist perspectives towards violence have always been controversial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter1978320_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter1978320-126">[123]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anarcho-pacifists" title="Anarcho-pacifists">Anarcho-pacifists</a> advocate for non-violence means to achieve their stateless, nonviolent ends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFiala2017section_3.1_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFiala2017section_3.1-127">[124]</a></sup> Other anarchist groups advocate direct action, a tactic which can include acts of <a href="/wiki/Sabotage" title="Sabotage">sabotage</a> or terrorism. This attitude was quite prominent a century ago when seeing the state as a <a href="/wiki/Tyrant" title="Tyrant">tyrant</a> and some anarchists believing that they had every right to oppose its <a href="/wiki/Oppression" title="Oppression">oppression</a> by any means possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinna2019116–117_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinna2019116–117-128">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Emma_Goldman" title="Emma Goldman">Emma Goldman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Errico_Malatesta" title="Errico Malatesta">Errico Malatesta</a>, who were proponents of limited use of violence, stated that violence is merely a reaction to state violence as a <a href="/wiki/Necessary_evil" title="Necessary evil">necessary evil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarter1978320–325_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarter1978320–325-129">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>Anarchists took an active role in <a href="/wiki/Strike_action" title="Strike action">strike actions</a>, although they tended to be antipathetic to formal <a href="/wiki/Syndicalism" title="Syndicalism">syndicalism</a>, seeing it as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformist" title="Reformist">reformist</a>. They saw it as a part of the movement which sought to overthrow the <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019113_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019113-130">[127]</a></sup> Anarchists also reinforced their propaganda within the arts, some of whom practiced <a href="/wiki/Naturism" title="Naturism">naturism</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nudism" title="Nudism">nudism</a>. Those anarchists also built communities which were based on <a href="/wiki/Friendship" title="Friendship">friendship</a> and were involved in the <a href="/wiki/News_media" title="News media">news media</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019114_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019114-131">[128]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolutionary">Revolutionary</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Black_bloc_at_RNC_running.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Black_bloc_at_RNC_running.jpg/220px-Black_bloc_at_RNC_running.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Black_bloc_at_RNC_running.jpg/330px-Black_bloc_at_RNC_running.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Black_bloc_at_RNC_running.jpg/440px-Black_bloc_at_RNC_running.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Black_bloc_at_RNC_running.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Black bloc protesters parading anarcho-communism imagery such as the motto "<a href="/wiki/No_War_but_the_Class_War" title="No War but the Class War">No War but the Class War</a>"</div></div></div>
<p>In the current era, Italian anarchist <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Bonanno" title="Alfredo Bonanno">Alfredo Bonanno</a>, a proponent of <a href="/wiki/Insurrectionary_anarchism" title="Insurrectionary anarchism">insurrectionary anarchism</a>, has reinstated the debate on violence by rejecting the nonviolence tactic adopted since the late 19th century by Kropotkin and other prominent anarchists afterwards. Both Bonanno and the French group <a href="/wiki/The_Invisible_Committee" title="The Invisible Committee">The Invisible Committee</a> advocate for small, informal affiliation groups, where each member is responsible for their own actions but works together to bring down oppression utilizing sabotage and other violent means against state, capitalism, and other enemies. Members of The Invisible Committee were arrested in 2008 on various charges, terrorism included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKinna2019134–135_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKinna2019134–135-132">[129]</a></sup>
</p><p>Overall, contemporary anarchists are much less violent and militant than their ideological ancestors. They mostly engage in confronting the police during demonstrations and riots, especially in countries such as <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_Canada" title="Anarchism in Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_Greece" title="Anarchism in Greece">Greece</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_Mexico" title="Anarchism in Mexico">Mexico</a>. Militant <a href="/wiki/Black_bloc" title="Black bloc">black bloc</a> protest groups are known for clashing with the police;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019115_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019115-133">[130]</a></sup> however, anarchists not only clash with state operators, they also engage in the struggle against fascists and racists, taking <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-fascist" title="Anti-fascist">anti-fascist</a> action and mobilizing to prevent hate rallies from happening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019117_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams2019117-134">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolutionary">Evolutionary</span></h3>
